1 The Simple Linear Regression Model

1.3 Plot Data

plot(food)         # Plot matrix

1.4 Model

\[ Y_{i} = \alpha + \beta X_{i} + e_{i} \]

1.5 Variables

x = food[,2]   # Income
y = food[,1]   # Food Expenditure

1.6 Estimation

reg <- lm(y ~ x)

1.7 Results

1.8 b1, b2

b1 <- coef(reg)[[1]] 
b2 <- coef(reg)[[2]]

b1
## [1] 83.416
b2
## [1] 10.20964

1.9 Least sqaures prediction (one time)

N <- 40
sde <- 89.52
y1 <- b1+b2*x+rnorm(N, mean=0, sd=sde)

y2 <- data.frame()
y2 <- cbind(y1, y)

1.10 Least sqaures prediction (one time)

matplot(y1, type='l', col=1:40,
        xlab='Income', ylab='Food Expenditure', 
        main ='Prediction N=1 ')

1.11 Least sqaures prediction (one time)

matplot(y2, type='l', col=1:40,
        xlab='Income', ylab='Food Expenditure', 
        main ='Food Expenditure vs. Prediction ')

1.12 Least sqaures prediction (1,000 times)

b1 <- coef(reg)[[1]] 
b2 <- coef(reg)[[2]]
yy <- data.frame()

trial <- 1
trials <- 1000
while(trial <= trials) {
  y3 <- b1+b2*x+rnorm(N, mean=0, sd=sde)
  yy <- rbind(yy, t(y3))
  trial <- trial + 1
}

1.13 Least sqaures prediction (1,000 times)

matplot(t(yy), type='l', col=1:40,
        xlab='Income', ylab='Food Expenditure', 
        main ='Prediction N=1000 ')

1.14 Save DATA

sink(‘ch4.out’)
